This is a great recipe. I now make these every week. I changed to suit my family's taste. No raisins, add unsweetened dried coconut, chopped pecans and a few chocolate chips. I sub flaxmeal for the wheat germ since I have that on hand. I use coconut oil instead of vegetable.  I also used old fashioned, not quick oats. I've make several variations and they have all been great. I usually up the quantity of some of the ingredients and have found that an extra egg and some water  help make the mixture wet enough that it holds together better. Thank you for  a great alternative to boxed granola bars.

text:
While not being the healthiest granola recipe this is a good one! Just be careful with your cooking times and you'll have chewy bars for ages, I only bake them for 15-20 mins at gas mark 4 otherwise they burn and become dry.  I make mine with linseed mix (flax) instead of wheatgerm and swap raisins for dried cranberries or whatever else I have to hand.  I've found the secret to making these my own by adding dried coconut, it gives the bars more texture.  If I'm being unhealthy I'll also add 50g of chocolate chips too!

I love this recipe and in fact have made this twice this week.  The only thing I'll note is that I suggest you watch the baking time.  My oven tends to run cooler than it says and using the recommended time the bars were a little too brown. BUT that's easy to fix.  I think this is a marvelously versatile recipe.  The second time I made it with chocolate chips.  I plan to make it again next week (which will be the third time in two weeks) with marshmallow fluff.  Sort of a rice crispy-playground bar hybrid.  Experimenting is fun.  You'll want to try cranberries and more because this is just a great useful recipe.  I glad they shared it.  [ps--I used extra extra virgin olive oil. Because it's healthy :]

city:

country:
None
text:
This is an awesome granola bar recipe.  It's easy for my toddler to help me dump the stuff in the bowl, and they are supper tummy and can be easily altered to what you have on hand.  I personally use melted butter instead of oil, because that's what I had the first time and like it in comparison.  I always go light on oatmeal and flour because I add chia seeds and an extra "fun" ingredient.  Always the raisins though.  My favorite combo so far was adding white chocolate chips and well crumbled graham crackers instead of flour.  I also ran out of honey, so I added some more brown sugar and whole milk at the end, just enough to get ingredients a little wet.  I also found baking this at 330 helps not burn anything.  Don't overlook it either, that helps them stay chewier.  I also think cutting them in squares as opposed to bars helps cut down on crumbles.  As directions say...watched until the just turn brown on edges, take it out.  Wait 5-7 minutes.  I then turn them over on a cutting board after releasing the edges with a knife.  I pat the bars so they are sticking together, then I wait five more minutes and then cut it with super sharp knife in squares.  You can obviously cut it however you want, I just found this way has less crumbs.  Parchment paper would also be a really good idea.

text:
This is one of my favorite recipes.  It is extremely versatile--today, I mixed in dried cranberries, walnuts, sunflower seeds, and mini chocolate chips.  Once you have made the recipe a couple of times and know what the texture is supposed to feel like before you bake it, you can start playing with the wet ingredients too.  I usually do an egg, some applesauce, plain yogurt, and a little bit of vegetable oil (not the full 1/2c, because you won't need it). Today I substituted coconut oil, but the bars are still baking so I can't say how that will taste.  I also either omit or greatly reduce the brown sugar, since I include chocolate chips and dried fruit for sweetness. Mine usually cook in less than 20 minutes, since I like chewy bars.  Recipe is delicious as written and it's really hard to mess up.

text:
WOW!!!! This recipes is exactly what I wanted. And it is so delicious! Like most other users, I made a few alterations to the original recipe: I used about 2/3 cup brown sugar, 1/4 wheat bran and 1/4 cup flax seed (in place of the wheat germ), 1 teaspoon ground cinnamon, 1 cup whole wheat flour instead of all-purpose flour, about 1/3 cup of honey, and I added about 1/2 each of raisins and dried cranberries. I sprinkled sliced raw almonds on the top ar well. I also only baked it for about 26 minutes (based on other's comments) and they were very chewy, almost a sticky granola texture, and they didn't form bars because of this. Next time I make this, I will probably bake it for 30 minutes in a 9 by 9 baking pan, just to get a thicker bar. Very, very good though. Highly recommended.

text:
I used flax instead of wheat germ since I didn't have any. I measured out the 1/2 cup, then ground half of that in my coffee grinder and left the rest whole; probably used more like a full cup this way. I used a cup of dried cranberries instead of 3/4 cup of raisins, since I didn't have any. I added 1/3 cup of unsweetened coconut flakes. I reduced the cinnamon to 1/2 teaspoon. so it wouldn't overpower the other flavours. I believe the bars came out crumbly as opposed to chewy because of the increased amount of dry ingredients; hence reducing the brown sugar by half and upping the honey would keep relatively the same amount of sweetness while binding them better.

Very yummy, and when I give these to my family, I KNOW what is in them!  And it's not preservatives and additives.  Thanks for the great recipe!

text:
These are great, very versatile.  I've made them many times.  I cut the brown sugar to 1/2 cup, use half whole wheat pastry flour, and use dried figs or dried apples in place of raisins (I hate raisins).  I add 1/2 cup walnuts or pecans and will sometimes use half flaxseed meal/half wheat germ.  They always turn out great and keep well for a few days.  I put them in the freezer if it's going to be longer than that.

text:
Great recipe!  I have made this several times now, each successfully!  I would like to note that I get the best results when I bake these in a glass (Pyrex) pan.  I have also varied the recipe by substituting the 1/2 c. honey with 1/2 c. peanut butter and adding chocolate chips.  The mixture will seem dry and you will have to mix it with your hands until it's all uniform, but once you bake it, it will turn out beautifully!  I have also made the basic recipe with ground almonds and raisins.

I wasnt that impressed when I first tasted them. But when they cooled, and I ate 5 bars, I decided I liked them alot! I cooked them for 20 mins. Definately long enough!  I think this is a good base recipe that you could alter MANY different ways and not mess up. I used 1/2 ap flour and 1/2 wheat. I didnt have wheat germ so I used part flax seed and part wheat bran.  I used SPlenda brown sugar instead. I used dates instead of raisins. Based on other's suggestions, I cut them while they were hot and stored in plastic container. Still soft day after. I am not a huge granola bar fan, but do like oatmeal. Really enjoyed these bars.

My husband loves to eat healthy, so experimenting with desserts isn't great all the time.  But THESE! I'm a longtime allrecipes user, but never registered until now. The main reason was so I could comment on how much I love this easy, delicious recipe. Like other commenters noted, so fun to add different components. My favorite combination thus far consists of unsalted peanuts, raisins and a few mini chocolate chips (to keep the boyfriend happy). I've been bragging about this recipe all week to friends and family. It's definitely a keeper!

text:
This is a great recipe!  I am always looking for healthy recipes to try, and this is the first granola bar recipe that I have been truly happy with.  It's so easy to midify!  They are a little sweet for me, however.  I've made these twice, and the second time was my favorite so far:  I substituted applesauce for half the oil, used 5-grain hot cereal for the oatmeal, whole wheat flour for all purpose, cornmeal for the wheat germ (didn't have any), added only about a third of the sugar called for, and used only 1 tsp of vanilla.  I found that the first time I made them, the vanilla came through a little too strong, but that could have been because I used all applesauce in place of oil and didn't add the brown sugar.  I also found that when using applesauce, if you like a crispier bar like I do, it's best to bake it for 5-10 minutes more than the recipe says.  Overall, though, this recipe is awesome, exactly what I was looking for!  Thanks!

text:
The beauty of this recipe is the ability to alter to your liking.  So I cut the oats to 1 1/2 cups and added 1 1/2 cups of Organic Flax Seed Pumpkin Cereal (no reason, just saw it in the store and though it would be a good addition)  so then I omitted the wheat germ and also the salt.  Kept all the wet ingredients the same plus added 1/2 c each of golden raisins, coconut, chocolate chips and finely chopped slivered almonds.  When I thought they were done baking, I cut them in the pan before they cooled but could tell they would crumble so I scored them and put them back in the oven to continue baking - sorta like with biscotti.   I placed the bars on a baking rack to continue cooling.  These were delicious,  I know I will be making them often!

I thought these were great but very sweet even though I reduced the brown sugar to 1/4 cup. I think next time I will cut the sugar out entirely and just use the honey and maybe reduce that as well. I added almonds and cherry flavored crasins because I hate rasins. I also used alcohol free vanilla syrup(kind of like extract but in syrup form and nice flavor) from the brand Fairtrade and that added more flavor. I used whole wheat flour also and added about half a cup of unsweetened applesauce which I think gave it a very nice chewy texture. Once they came out the oven I waited 5 minutes and cut this into bars and immediately wrapped them in plastic wrap to keep it chewy and moist. The end result with the above changes made this a 5 but as is this is a 4. Thank you preggomom!

These were pretty good, but I made some major changes. I used 1 cup of rolled oats and 1 cup Kashi brand GoLean cereal, added some raw almonds, 1/2 cup packed brown sugar, 1 tsp cinnamon, 1 cup whole wheat flour, 1/2 cup of cranberries (raisins give my dad gas, ha ha), and replaced vegetable oil with canola oil. The only thing I would change next time would be to eliminate the salt in the recipe altogether. They taste a little bit too salty, otherwise. Other than that, they came out really well, and are packed with protein thanks to the wheat germ and Kashi cereal (which contains 13 grams of protein per cup)

text:
SO YUMMY! I'd been using a no-bake recipe from this site until it mysteriously disappeared and was looking for a replacement - this is it! Because granola bar recipes tend to be endlessly forgiving, I made substitutions as I saw fit - used soy flour in place of 1/3 of the regular flour; used oat bran instead of wheat bran (heart healthy!); added 1/4 tsp nutmeg; craisins instead of raisins; and added walnuts and uncooked millet (my girlfriend's idea) for extra yummy crunch! As others mentioned, I cooked mine only about 25 minutes and they turned out perfect. I love how these are lighter than ones that call for peanut butter and chocolate (although I'm sure you could add those if you like). Great recipe, my new go-to - thanks!

This is a great base recipe to have. I'd been looking for a way to use the excess of oatmeal I'd stockpiled in the back of my pantry. Quick to prepare, too. text:
I make these granola bars a lot, with the following alterations:

- add 1/2 cup wheat bran
- add a second egg
- hold the cinnamon and raisins
- add 1/2 cup sunflower seeds or pecan pieces
- add 1/2 cup bittersweet chocolate chips
- always used buckwheat honey

I bake until they are downright crispy around the edges.  They make a great breakfast on the go!
